target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 1</span></a>\n              <p>Color image of A1689 obtained by combining <i>F475W</i>, <i>F775W</i>, and <i>F850LP </i>HST/ACS images using a logarithmic scale. The footprint of the MUSE field is displayed together with the sources spectroscopically identified in this field: cluster galaxies (red), stars (magenta), background galaxies at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8804; 3</span> (cyan), and <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8805; 3</span> (yellow). Cluster galaxies that were manually extracted are labeled CG. Objects labeled LN correspond to either line emitters or multiple images lacking a counterpart in the reference catalog based on the <i>F775W </i>image (see text for details). North is up, east is left. A tentative spectroscopic redshift was also obtained for the long southeast arcs in this field, namely 8a and 8b in C10 (see discussion in Sect. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#S8\">4.1</a>). At the redshift of the cluster, the MUSE field is equivalent to <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span><span class=\"simple-math\">185 &#215; 185</span> kpc.</p>\n            </td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\" class=\"in-txt\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F1\">In the text</a></td></tr>\n</table></div>\n<div class=\"inset\"><table>\n<tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F2.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15-fig2_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F2.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 2</span></a>\n            <p>Histogram showing the velocity distribution for the 63 cluster galaxies found in the MUSE field of view with respect to the centroid for the whole distribution (<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 0.1891</span>). Solid lines display the best Gaussian fit to the whole sample. Long and short dashed lines display the best fit to the main cluster component (low-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i></span>) and the northeast group (high-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i></span>), respectively.</p>\n          </td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\" class=\"in-txt\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F2\">In the text</a></td></tr>\n</table></div>\n<div class=\"inset\"><table>\n<tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F3.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15-fig3_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F3.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 3</span></a>\n            <p>Extracted spectra of all multiply imaged systems identified in the MUSE field of view at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8804; 3</span>, ordered according to increasing redshift, following the identifications in Table <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#T2\">2</a>. of Geneva, 51 chemin des Maillettes, 1290 Versoix, Switzerland\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_title\" content=\"MUSE observations of the lensing cluster Abell 1689\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_online_date\" content=\"2016/04/28\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_publication_date\" content=\"2016/06/01\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_volume\" content=\"590\">\n  <meta content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/pdf/2016/06/aa27913-15.pdf\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_issn\" content=\"0004-6361\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_issn\" content=\"1432-0746\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_language\" content=\"en\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"gravitational lensing: strong\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"galaxies: high-redshift\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"galaxies: clusters: individual: Abell 1689\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_article_type\" content=\"Research Article\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_abstract\" lang=\"en\" content=\"&lt;i&gt;Context. &lt;i/&gt;This paper presents the results obtained with the Multi Unit Spectroscopic Explorer (MUSE) for the core of the lensing cluster Abell 1689, as part of MUSE\u2019s commissioning at the ESO Very Large Telescope.&lt;i&gt;Aims. &lt;i/&gt;Integral-field observations with MUSE provide a unique view of the central 1 \u00d7 1 arcmin&lt;sup&gt;2&lt;sup/&gt; region at intermediate spectral resolution in the visible domain, allowing us to conduct a complete census of both cluster galaxies and lensed background sources.&lt;i&gt;Methods. &lt;i/&gt;We performed a spectroscopic analysis of all sources found in the MUSE data cube. Two hundred and eighty-two objects were systematically extracted from the cube based on a guided-and-manual approach. We also tested three different tools for the automated detection and extraction of line emitters. Cluster galaxies and lensed sources were identified based on their spectral features. We investigated the multiple-image configuration for all known sources in the field. &lt;i&gt;Results. &lt;i/&gt;Previous to our survey, 28 different lensed galaxies displaying 46 multiple images were known in the MUSE field of view, most of them were detected through photometric redshifts and lensing considerations. Of these, we spectroscopically confirm 12 images based on their emission lines, corresponding to 7 different lensed galaxies between &lt;i&gt;z&lt;i/&gt; = 0.95 and 5.0. In addition, 14 new galaxies have been spectroscopically identified in this area thanks to MUSE data, with redshifts ranging between 0.8 and 6.2. All background sources detected within the MUSE field of view correspond to multiple-imaged systems lensed by A1689. Seventeen sources in total are found at &lt;i&gt;z&lt;i/&gt; \u2265 3 based on their Lyman-&lt;i&gt;\u03b1&lt;i/&gt; emission, with Lyman-&lt;i&gt;\u03b1&lt;i/&gt; luminosities ranging between 40.5 \u2272 log\u2009(Ly&lt;i&gt;\u03b1&lt;i/&gt;) \u2272 42.5 after correction for magnification. This sample is particularly sensitive to the slope of the luminosity function toward the faintest end. The density of sources obtained in this survey is consistent with a steep value of &lt;i&gt;\u03b1&lt;i/&gt; \u2264 \u22121.5, although this result still needs further investigation. &lt;i&gt;Conclusions. &lt;i/&gt;These results illustrate the efficiency of MUSE in characterizing lensing clusters on one hand and in studying faint and distant populations of galaxies on the other hand. In particular, our current survey of lensing clusters is expected to provide a unique census of sources responsible for the reionization in a representative volume at &lt;i&gt;z&lt;i/&gt; ~ 4\u22127.\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_reference\" content=\"citation_author=A. Bina</span><sup>1</sup><sup>,2</sup>, <span id=\"aa27913-15-author-2\" data-url=\"/component/author/?dkey=10.1051/0004-6361/201527913&amp;n=2\" class=\"author\">R. Pell&#243;</span><sup>1</sup><sup>,2</sup>, <span id=\"aa27913-15-author-3\" data-url=\"/component/author/?dkey=10.1051/0004-6361/201527913&amp;n=3\" class=\"author\">J. Richard</span><sup>3</sup>, <span id=\"aa27913-15-author-4\" data-url=\"/component/author/?dkey=10.1051/0004-6361/201527913&amp;n=4\" class=\"author\">J. Lewis</span><sup>1</sup><sup>,2</sup>, <span id=\"aa27913-15-author-5\" data-url=\"/component/author/?dkey=10.1051/0004-6361/201527913&amp;n=5\" class=\"author\">V. Patr&#237;cio</span><sup>3</sup>, <span id=\"aa27913-15-author-6\" data-url=\"/component/author/?dkey=10.1051/0004-6361/201527913&amp;n=6\" class=\"author\">S. Cantalupo</span><sup>4</sup>, <span id=\"aa27913-15-author-7\" data-url=\"/component/author/?dkey=10.1051/0004-6361/201527913&amp;n=7\" class=\"author\">E. C. Herenz</span><sup>5</sup>, <span id=\"aa27913-15-author-8\" data-url=\"/component/author/?dkey=10.1051/0004-6361/201527913&amp;n=8\" class=\"author\">K. Soto</span><sup>4</sup>, <span id=\"aa27913-15-author-9\" data-url=\"/component/author/?dkey=10.1051/0004-6361/201527913&amp;n=9\" class=\"author\">P. M. Weilbacher</span><sup>5</sup>, <span id=\"aa27913-15-author-10\" data-url=\"/component/author/?dkey=10.1051/0004-6361/201527913&amp;n=10\" class=\"author\">R. Bacon</span><sup>3</sup>, <span id=\"aa27913-15-author-11\" data-url=\"/component/author/?dkey=10.1051/0004-6361/201527913&amp;n=11\" class=\"author\">J. D. R. Vernet</span><sup>6</sup>, <span id=\"aa27913-15-author-12\" data-url=\"/component/author/?dkey=10.1051/0004-6361/201527913&amp;n=12\" class=\"author\">L. Wisotzki</span><sup>5</sup>, <span id=\"aa27913-15-author-13\" data-url=\"/component/author/?dkey=10.1051/0004-6361/201527913&amp;n=13\" class=\"author\">B. Cl&#233;ment</span><sup>3</sup>, <span id=\"aa27913-15-author-14\" data-url=\"/component/author/?dkey=10.1051/0004-6361/201527913&amp;n=14\" class=\"author\">J. G. Cuby</span><sup>7</sup>, <span id=\"aa27913-15-author-15\" data-url=\"/component/author/?dkey=10.1051/0004-6361/201527913&amp;n=15\" class=\"author\">D. J. Lagattuta</span><sup>3</sup>, <span id=\"aa27913-15-author-16\" data-url=\"/component/author/?dkey=10.1051/0004-6361/201527913&amp;n=16\" class=\"author\">G. Soucail</span><sup>1</sup><sup>,2</sup> and <span id=\"aa27913-15-author-17\" data-url=\"/component/author/?dkey=10.1051/0004-6361/201527913&amp;n=17\" class=\"author\">A. Verhamme</span><sup>3</sup><sup>,8</sup></p></div>\n<p class=\"aff\">\n          <sup>1</sup> \n          Universit&#233; de Toulouse, UPS-OMP, IRAP,   31400 \n             Toulouse,\n             France \n          \n        <br>\n            e-mail: dbina@irap.omp.eu; rpello@irap.omp.eu\n          <br>\n          <sup>2</sup> \n          CNRS, IRAP, 14,\n              avenue &#201;douard Belin,  31400 \n             Toulouse,\n             France \n        <br>\n          <sup>3</sup> \n          Univ. Lyon, Univ. Lyon1, ENS de Lyon, CNRS, Centre de Recherche\n              Astrophysique de Lyon UMR 5574,  69230 \n             Saint-Genis-Laval,\n               France \n        <br>\n          <sup>4</sup> \n          ETH Zurich, Institute of Astronomy, Wolfgang-Pauli-Str. 27,  8093 \n             Zurich,\n               Switzerland \n        <br>\n          <sup>5</sup> \n           Leibniz-Institut f&#252;r Astrophysik Potsdam (AIP),\n               An der Sternwarte 16,\n               14482 \n             Potsdam,\n             Germany \n        <br>\n          <sup>6</sup> \n           European Southern Observatory,  Karl Schwarzschild Stra&#223;e 2,  85748 \n             Garching,\n             Germany \n        <br>\n          <sup>7</sup> \n          Aix-Marseille Universit&#233;, CNRS, LAM (Laboratoire d&#8217;Astrophysique\n              de Marseille) UMR 7326,  13388 \n             Marseille,\n             France \n        <br>\n          <sup>8</sup> \n          Geneva Observatory, University of Geneva,\n               51 chemin des Maillettes,\n               1290 \n             Versoix,\n               Switzerland \n        <br></p>\n<p class=\"history\"><span class=\"bold\">Received: </span>7 December 2015<br><span class=\"bold\">Accepted: </span>7 March 2016</p>\n<p class=\"bold\"><a name=\"abs\"></a>Abstract</p>\n        <p><i>Context. </i>This paper presents the results obtained with the Multi Unit Spectroscopic Explorer (MUSE) for the core of the lensing cluster Abell 1689, as part of MUSE&#8217;s commissioning at the ESO Very Large Telescope.</p>\n        <p><i>Aims. </i>Integral-field observations with MUSE provide a unique view of the central 1 <span class=\"simple-math\">&#215;</span> 1 arcmin<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span> region at intermediate spectral resolution in the visible domain, allowing us to conduct a complete census of both cluster galaxies and lensed background sources.</p>\n        <p><i>Methods. </i>We performed a spectroscopic analysis of all sources found in the MUSE data cube. Two hundred and eighty-two objects were systematically extracted from the cube based on a guided-and-manual approach. We also tested three different tools for the automated detection and extraction of line emitters. Cluster galaxies and lensed sources were identified based on their spectral features. We investigated the multiple-image configuration for all known sources in the field. </p>\n        <p><i>Results. </i>Previous to our survey, 28 different lensed galaxies displaying 46 multiple images were known in the MUSE field of view, most of them were detected through photometric redshifts and lensing considerations. Of these, we spectroscopically confirm 12 images based on their emission lines, corresponding to 7 different lensed galaxies between <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> =</span> 0.95 and 5.0. In addition, 14 new galaxies have been spectroscopically identified in this area thanks to MUSE data, with redshifts ranging between 0.8 and 6.2. All background sources detected within the MUSE field of view correspond to multiple-imaged systems lensed by A1689. Seventeen sources in total are found at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8805; 3</span> based on their Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emission, with Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> luminosities ranging between <span class=\"simple-math\">40.5 &#8818; log&#8201;(Ly<i>&#945;</i>) &#8818; 42.5</span> after correction for magnification. This sample is particularly sensitive to the slope of the luminosity function toward the faintest end. The density of sources obtained in this survey is consistent with a steep value of <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i> &#8804; &#8722;1.5</span>, although this result still needs further investigation. </p>\n        <p><i>Conclusions. </i>These results illustrate the efficiency of MUSE in characterizing lensing clusters on one hand and in studying faint and distant populations of galaxies on the other hand. In particular, our current survey of lensing clusters is expected to provide a unique census of sources responsible for the reionization in a representative volume at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> ~ 4&#8722;7</span>. </p>\n      <div class=\"kword\"><p><span class=\"bold\">Key words: </span>gravitational lensing: strong / galaxies: high-redshift / galaxies: clusters: individual: Abell 1689</p></div>\n</div>\n<p><i>&#169; ESO, 2016</i></p>\n<h2 class=\"sec\">\n<a name=\"S1\"></a>1. Introduction</h2>\n<p>Clusters of galaxies are recognized to be the most efficient gravitational lenses in the Universe <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2011A&amp;ARv..19...47K\" target=\"_blank\">(see, e.g., Kneib &amp; Natarajan 2011, and the references therein)</a>. For almost 30 years since their discovery, they have allowed the astrophysical community to detect extremely faint and distant sources that would otherwise be inaccessible. Strong magnification in the core of lensing clusters has opened a brand-new type of observational approach to characterize the most distant or faint sources while reducing the selection bias in luminosity. Many high-redshift sources have been identified and studied using this approach during the last years <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2012Natur.489..406Z,%202013ApJ...762...32C,%202015A&amp;A...575A..92L,%202015ApJ...800...18A\" target=\"_blank\">(see, e.g., Zheng et al. 2012; Coe et al. 2013; Laporte et al. 2015; Atek et al. 2015)</a>. Cluster lenses have also contributed to constrain the luminosity function for galaxies at high-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i></span> down to the faintest limits, often through dedicated surveys <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2014ApJ...792...76B,%202015ApJ...799...12I,%202015ApJ...800...18A\" target=\"_blank\">(Bradley et al. 2014; Ishigaki et al. 2015; Atek et al. 2015)</a>. Using lensing clusters as efficient gravitational telescopes requires a detailed knowledge of the mass distribution, which in turn depends on the correct identification of multiply imaged systems in the cluster core <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2011MNRAS.410.1939Z,%202014MNRAS.444..268R\" target=\"_blank\">(Zitrin et al. 2011; Richard et al. 2014)</a>. </p>\n<p>This paper presents the results obtained with the Multi Unit Spectroscopic Explorer <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2010SPIE.7735E..08B\" target=\"_blank\">(MUSE Bacon et al. 2010)</a> of the core of the lensing cluster Abell 1689 (hereafter A1689), as part of MUSE&#8217;s commissioning at the ESO Very Large Telescope. This cluster has been extensively studied during the past 20 years because it is one of the most efficient strong-lensing clusters currently known. Previous analysis of A1689 discovered a large number of multiple images. <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2010ApJ...723.1678C\" target=\"_blank\">Coe et al. (2010, hereafter C10)</a> used 135 images of 42 galaxies identified within the central <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>400 kpc diameter region to constrain their mass model. One of the most spectacular cases of a strong-lensing configuration are the Sextet Arcs, discovered in this cluster by <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2007ApJ...665..921F\" target=\"_blank\">Frye et al. (2007)</a>, and produced by a <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 3.038</span> Lyman-break galaxy (LBG). The large number of multiple images identified in this field has allowed a reliable mass reconstruction for this cluster, making it one of the best-known gravitational telescopes <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2007ApJ...668..643L,%202008MNRAS.386.1169T,%202010ApJ...723.1678C\" target=\"_blank\">(see, e.g., Limousin et al. 2007; Tu et al. 2008; Coe et al. 2010)</a>. For this reason, A1689 has become a privileged line of sight along which to study the properties of faint and distant samples of background galaxies <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2014ApJ...780..143A\" target=\"_blank\">(Alavi et al. 2014)</a>. </p>\n<p>Integral-field observations of A1689 with MUSE provide a unique view of the central 1 <span class=\"simple-math\">&#215;</span> 1 arcmin<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span> region at intermediate spectral resolution in the visible domain, allowing us to conduct a complete census of both cluster galaxies and lensed background sources, in particular in the <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> ~ 2.7&#8722;6.5</span> domain. Our performance assessment of MUSE in the field of A1689 confirms the idea that this instrument is particularly well suited for the study of faint and distant populations of galaxies <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2015MNRAS.446L..16R,%202015A&amp;A...575A..75B\" target=\"_blank\">(see also Richard et al. 2015; Bacon et al. 2015)</a>. </p>\n<p>The outline of this article is as follows. In Sect. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#S2\">2</a> we describe the observations carried out on the field of A1689 and provide a summary of the data reduction and analysis process. Section <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#S6\">3</a> addresses the properties of the cluster galaxy populations as seen by MUSE. The identification of background sources lensed by A1689 is discussed in Sect. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#S7\">4</a>, in particular the spectroscopic confirmation of known multiply imaged sources as well as the discovery of new multiple systems. Implications of these results on the mass modeling of A1689 are also discussed in this section. Conclusions and perspectives are given in Sect. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#S11\">5</a>. Throughout this paper, we adopt a <span class=\"simple-math\">&#923;</span>-CDM cosmology with <span class=\"simple-math\">&#937;<sub>&#923;</sub> = 0.7</span>, <span class=\"simple-math\">&#937;<sub>m</sub> = 0.3</span> and <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>H</i><sub>0</sub> = 70</span> km&#8201;s<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>-1</sup></span>&#8201;Mpc<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>-1</sup></span>. Magnitudes are given in the AB system <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/1983ApJ...266..713O\" target=\"_blank\">(Oke &amp; Gunn 1983)</a>. All quoted redshift measurements are based on vacuum rest-frame wavelengths unless otherwise specified. </p>\n<h2 class=\"sec\">\n<a name=\"S2\"></a>2. From MUSE data to source extraction</h2>\n<h3 class=\"sec2\">\n<a name=\"S3\"></a>2.1. Observations and data reduction</h3>\n<p>The core of A1689 <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/1990ApJS...72..715T\" target=\"_blank\">(z=0.1847, Teague et al. 1990)</a> was targeted with MUSE during its first commissioning run on February 9, 2014 (ESO program 60.A-9100(A)). We observed a single field of view, centered on <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i> = 13:11:30.5</span>, <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#948;</i> = &#8722;01:20:41.5</span> (J2000) and oriented at PA = 0<span class=\"simple-math\">&#176;</span>, covering a field of view of about 1 <span class=\"simple-math\">&#215;</span> 1 arcmin<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span> (<span class=\"simple-math\">~</span><span class=\"simple-math\">185 &#215; 185</span> kpc at the redshift of the cluster). The total exposure time was <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>1.83 h, divided into six individual exposures of 1100 s of integration time with a small linear dither pattern of 0.2<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span> and no rotation between each exposure. Observations were obtained in the nominal WFM-NOAO-N mode of MUSE, in good seeing conditions ranging between <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>0.51<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span> and 0.87<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span>, as measured by the DIMM seeing monitor, and between <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>0.9<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span> and 1.1<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span> (FWHM) as measured from MUSE data cubes in the reconstructed white-light images. </p>\n<p>MUSE data were reduced using the MUSE Data Reduction System V1.0 (<a name=\"InR38\"></a><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#R38\">Weilbacher et al. 2012</a>, <a name=\"InR39\"></a><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#R39\">2014</a>), including bias, dark, flat-fielding, and geometrical corrections, basic sky subtraction, wavelength and flux calibrations, and astrometry. The six individual exposures were reduced and combined into a final datacube. Sky subtraction and correction for sky residuals were performed with the ZAP software <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2016MNRAS.tmp..248S\" target=\"_blank\">(Zurich Atmoshere Purge Soto et al. 2016)</a>. Several versions of the MUSE datacube were performed, with different choices for the combination parameters and the correction for sky residuals. Flux calibration and telluric correction was achieved based on observations of the standard star HD 49798 (O6 star). The final datacubes extend between 4750 and 9351 <span class=\"simple-math\">&#197;</span>, that is, 3681 spectral pixels with a scaling of 1.25 <span class=\"simple-math\">&#197;</span>/pixel and a spatial scale of 0.2<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span>/pixel. The spectral resolving power varies between <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>2000 in the blue and 4000 in the red. The seeing measured on the combined exposure is <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>0.6<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span><i>FWHM</i> at 7300 <span class=\"simple-math\">&#197;</span>. </p>\n<p>In addition to MUSE data, we used archive observations obtained by the <i>Hubble </i>Space Telescope (HST) with ACS in the optical bands (<i>F475W</i>, <i>F625W</i>, <i>F775W</i>, <i>F850LP</i>; PID 9289, PI: H. Ford). These deep images reach a limiting magnitude of <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>AB</i> ~ 28.2</span> in the <i>F775W </i>filter (5<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#963;</i></span> in a 0.2<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span> radius aperture) <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2014ApJ...780..143A\" target=\"_blank\">(see also Alavi et al. 2014)</a>. Sources were extracted using two different approaches: a guided extraction based on the detection on HST images, and a blind detection of line-emitters using different automated tools. A color image of the HST field of view showing the footprint of the MUSE field is displayed in Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F1\">1</a>, together with the lensed sources that are spectroscopically identified or confirmed in this work. </p>\n<h3 class=\"sec2\">\n<a name=\"S4\"></a>2.2. Extraction of HST-detected sources</h3>\n<p>Sources were extracted using two different approaches. First, a catalog of objects was built with SExtractor package version 2.8 (<a name=\"InR5\"></a><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#R5\">Bertin &amp; Arnouts 1996</a>) based on the detection on the <i>F775W </i>image. Two hundred forty-five objects were detected in this way within the MUSE field of view, with Kron-like magnitudes (SExtractor MAG_AUTO) ranging between 17.0 and 28.1. Before extracting background sources in the central region from the MUSE cube, background residuals and continuum emission from bright cluster galaxies (hereafter BCGs) were fitted and removed from the MUSE cube with median filtering in both wavelength and spatial directions. The BCG area hereafter refers to the central region, which is strongly contaminated by the bright galaxies and displayed in a pink color-scale in Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F1\">1</a>. When building the catalog, ten bright sources in the cluster core that were missed by SExtractor because of severe crowding, were manually added. In addition, 23 multiple images from <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2010ApJ...723.1678C\" target=\"_blank\">Coe et al. (2010)</a> were missing from the SExtractor catalog for various reasons, mainly because they are located within or close to the central halo. They were also added to the catalog, as well as the four line emitters that were serendipitously discovered after manual inspection of the cube. This process provided 282 objects within the MUSE field of view. 1D spectra for all these sources were systematically extracted from the MUSE cube using a fixed aperture corresponding to 1.5<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span> diameter. </p>\n<p>Based on this guided-and-manual approach, a secure redshift could be determined for all sources up to MAG_AUTO <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>m</i></span>(775W) <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span> 21.5, most of them being cluster galaxies or stars identified based on their continuum emission. Redshifts were first measured based on manual inspection, followed by template fitting. In total, the spectroscopic sample obtained in this way over the entire photometric catalog yields 63 cluster galaxies (49 of them with <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>m</i></span>(775W) <span class=\"simple-math\">&lt;</span> 21.5), 5 stars, and 24 galaxies behind the cluster, 17 of them corresponding to sources at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8805; 3</span> detected by their Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emission. The majority of these <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8805; 3</span> identifications were verified manually and by lensing (see below). </p>\n<p>\n          \n          <a name=\"F1\"></a><div class=\"inset\"><table><tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F1.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15-fig1_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F1.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 1</span></a>\n              <p>Color image of A1689 obtained by combining <i>F475W</i>, <i>F775W</i>, and <i>F850LP </i>HST/ACS images using a logarithmic scale. The footprint of the MUSE field is displayed together with the sources spectroscopically identified in this field: cluster galaxies (red), stars (magenta), background galaxies at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8804; 3</span> (cyan), and <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8805; 3</span> (yellow). Cluster galaxies that were manually extracted are labeled CG. Objects labeled LN correspond to either line emitters or multiple images lacking a counterpart in the reference catalog based on the <i>F775W </i>image (see text for details). North is up, east is left. A tentative spectroscopic redshift was also obtained for the long southeast arcs in this field, namely 8a and 8b in C10 (see discussion in Sect. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#S8\">4.1</a>). At the redshift of the cluster, the MUSE field is equivalent to <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span><span class=\"simple-math\">185 &#215; 185</span> kpc.</p>\n            </td>\n</tr></table></div>\n        </p>\n<h3 class=\"sec2\">\n<a name=\"S5\"></a>2.3. Blind extraction of line emitters</h3>\n<p>The second approach was the automated (blind) detection and extraction of line emitters and continuum based on three main tools that are developed within the MUSE consortium, namely CubExtractor, LSDCat, and MUSELET. CubExtractor (Cantalupo, in prep.) detects and extracts sources as connected voxels (pixels in the cube) above a given pixel-to-pixel signal-to-noise ratio (S/N) threshold, after 3D Gaussian filtering of the MUSE datacube. LSDCat (Herenz, in prep.) is optimized for the extraction of compact narrow emission-line objects using a matched-filtering approach. MUSELET (for MUSE line-emission tracker, Richard, in prep.) is a simple SExtractor-based tool that extracts sources displaying line-emission, regardless of whether they are linked with continuum emission. All these tools have been optimized for the extraction of line emitters in different environments. Using them in this crowded field was particularly challenging. </p>\n<p>A systematic manual inspection was needed to exclude spurious detections, most of them coming from sky-line residuals or imperfect correction for cosmic rays (sometimes showing extended structure in the final cube). During this phase, we used three different versions of the MUSE datacube, with different choices in the parameters used for background subtraction, sky-line residuals and cosmic-ray corrections. Reliable emission lines are expected to be detected in all the cubes. The percentage of spurious detections depends on the flux level of the lines and the parameters used for the automated detection, typically ranging from a few percent for the brightest sources to as high as <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>75% for the faintest ones (e.g., flux <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span><span class=\"simple-math\">5 &#215; 10<sup>-18</sup></span> erg/s/cm<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>). </p>\n<p>These tools used in various combinations allowed us to detect 14 new emission-line objects, most of them lacking a clear counterpart in the HST/ACS images. All line emitters extracted based on the guided-and-manual approach and discussed in the previous section were detected by one of the automated tools. All sources retained in Sect. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#S7\">4</a> were found in all different versions of the MUSE data cubes (with and without background residuals and continuum emission subtracted). All of them yield multiple-image configurations in good agreement with lensing expectations. Based on our experience, the automated procedure was especially useful to find faint emission-line objects, with a typical flux of a few 10<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>-18</sup></span> erg/s/cm<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>, in particular those lacking a clear detection on HST/ACS images. </p>\n<h2 class=\"sec\">\n<a name=\"S6\"></a>3. Cluster galaxies</h2>\n<p>The spectroscopic sample obtained in the MUSE field includes 63 cluster galaxies with secure redshifts. All of them exhibit early-type spectra, excepted for two emission-line galaxies. Forty-nine of them are bright, that is, have <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>m</i></span>(775W) <span class=\"simple-math\">&lt;</span> 21.5. They constitute the majority of the sample within the spectroscopic completeness. Redshifts were measured based on the fit of several absorption lines with high S/N (Balmer series, MgI, Gband, etc.). The mean and the median redshifts for this sample are <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 0.1891</span> and 0.1889, respectively (<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 0.1883</span> and 0.1875 when the sample is limited to the completeness level at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>m</i></span>(775W) <span class=\"simple-math\">&#8804;</span> 21.5). When adopting the mean redshift for the whole sample as the heliocentric reference, the velocity dispersion is found to be <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#963;</i> = 2214 &#177; 38</span> km&#8201;s<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>-1</sup></span>, in good agreement with previous findings in the literature that used more galaxies and wider regions (typically a few Mpc) <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/1990ApJS...72..715T,%201991ApJS...77..363S\" target=\"_blank\">(see, e.g., Teague et al. 1990; Struble &amp; Rood 1991)</a> This value also agrees well with the largest spectroscopic survey conducted so far on this cluster by <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2004ogci.conf..183C\" target=\"_blank\">Czoske (2004)</a>, which included 525 cluster members and displayed a velocity dispersion profile decreasing from <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>2100 km&#8201;s<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>-1</sup></span> in the center to 1200 km&#8201;s<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>-1</sup></span> at <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>3 <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>h</i><sup>-1</sup></span>&#8201;Mpc from the core. Figure <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F2\">2</a> displays the velocity distribution found in the MUSE field of view with respect to the centroid of the whole distribution, and the best Gaussian fit. The velocity dispersion does not depend on the sample and the reference used (i.e., when the center of mass is computed based on either the whole sample or the bright sample alone), all <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#963;</i></span> values are the same within a <span class=\"simple-math\">&#177;</span>0.5% interval. </p>\n<p>\n        \n        <a name=\"F2\"></a><div class=\"inset\"><table><tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F2.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15-fig2_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F2.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 2</span></a>\n            <p>Histogram showing the velocity distribution for the 63 cluster galaxies found in the MUSE field of view with respect to the centroid for the whole distribution (<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 0.1891</span>). Solid lines display the best Gaussian fit to the whole sample. Long and short dashed lines display the best fit to the main cluster component (low-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i></span>) and the northeast group (high-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i></span>), respectively.</p>\n          </td>\n</tr></table></div>\n      </p>\n<p>\n        <a name=\"T1\"></a><div class=\"inset\"><div class=\"ligne\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/T1.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Table 1</span></a>\n            <p> Summary of the main parameters defining the lensing model. </p>\n          </div></div>\n      </p>\n<p>However, Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F2\">2</a> displays a more complex distribution than the smooth Gaussian distribution found for this cluster on larger scales. <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2004ogci.conf..183C\" target=\"_blank\">Czoske (2004)</a>, found no evidence for any substructure at <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>1 <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>h</i><sup>-1</sup></span>&#8201;Mpc scales, but a group of bright galaxies lies at <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>350 kpc northeast of the cluster center, therefore outside the MUSE field of view, but is still visible in the velocity distribution. This group is typically interpreted as evidence for a non-relaxed state in the cluster center that is possibly due to an ongoing merger <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2007ApJ...668..643L\" target=\"_blank\">(Limousin et al. 2007)</a>. This close group skews the redshift distribution toward slightly higher redshifts (<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8805; 0.195</span>) and broadens the redshift distribution in the cluster core. Figure <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F2\">2</a> also displays the best fit found when considering two independent components, the main cluster component with <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#963;</i> = 1200 &#177; 51</span> km&#8201;s<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>-1</sup></span>, and the group component with <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#963;</i> = 600 &#177; 68</span> km&#8201;s<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>-1</sup></span>. The velocity offset between the two subclumps is 4030 km&#8201;s<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>-1</sup></span>. As a consequence of this effect, the mean redshift is slightly biased toward a higher value than in previous findings, that is, a value close to <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 0.188</span> compared to <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 0.184</span> in the references given above. The redshift of the main cluster component is fully consistent with <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 0.184</span>. There is no obvious trend in the spatial distribution of galaxies belonging to the group across the MUSE field of view. </p>\n<p>We have also checked the consistency between our redshifts for galaxies in the center of the cluster with respect to existing data, being aware that spectroscopic targets were more sparsely sampled in previous surveys. Three galaxies of our sample are in common with <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/1990ApJS...72..715T\" target=\"_blank\">Teague et al. (1990)</a> (708, 710, and 711 in Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F1\">1</a>), and four galaxies with <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2004ogci.conf..183C\" target=\"_blank\">Czoske (2004, and private communication)</a>, (545, 713, 777, and 732 in Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F1\">1</a>). The average difference is consistent with zero: <span class=\"simple-math\">&#10216; d<i>z</i> &#10217;  = 0.0001 &#177; 0.001</span>. </p>\n<p>The results above show that MUSE is able to catch the small-scale substructure in particularly dense environments, a difficult task for standard multi-slit specrographs. This result supports the method adopted by <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2007ApJ...668..643L\" target=\"_blank\">Limousin et al. (2007, hereafter L07)</a> to optimize the lensing mass-modeling in this cluster, based on observations by <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2004ogci.conf..183C\" target=\"_blank\">Czoske (2004)</a> for the cluster dynamics and 32 multiply imaged systems known in this cluster at that epoch. They used a parametric reconstruction of the mass-distribution based on the superposition of two dominant dark-matter clumps, with <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#963;</i> = 1200</span> and 540 km&#8201;s<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>-1</sup></span>, respectively, to reproduce the large-scale component. A refined version of the L07 model is used in this paper (see Sect. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#S7\">4</a>). </p>\n<h2 class=\"sec\">\n<a name=\"S7\"></a>4. Lensed sources behind A1689</h2>\n<p>Previous to our survey, 28 different lensed galaxies displaying 46 multiple images were known in the MUSE field of view, most of them based on photometric redshifts together with lensing considerations <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2007ApJ...668..643L,%202007ApJ...665..921F,%202008MNRAS.386.1169T,%202010ApJ...723.1678C\" target=\"_blank\">(see, e.g., Limousin et al. 2007; Frye et al. 2007; Tu et al. 2008; Coe et al. 2010)</a>. Of these, we have been able to confirm 12 images corresponding to 7 different lensed galaxies between <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> =</span> 0.95 and 5.0. These systems are described in Sect. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#S8\">4.1</a>. Fourteen new galaxies have also been spectroscopically identified in this area thanks to MUSE data, with redshifts ranging between 0.8 and 6.2, as presented in Sect. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#S9\">4.2</a>. The majority of the lensed galaxies has been identified based on their Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emission. </p>\n<p>The lensing model used to analyze these data is the one presented in L07, based on Lenstool <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2007NJPh....9..447J\" target=\"_blank\">(Jullo et al. 2007)</a>, with some refinements to include the latest spectroscopic constraints on multiple images available in the literature for this cluster (see also Richard et al., in prep.). Table  <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#T1\">1</a> provides the updated version of Table 3 in L07, summarizing the main parameters used throughout this paper for the lensing model. Dark matter halos are modeled by a truncated pseudo-isothermal elliptical mass distribution scaled to their masses, from large-scales (clumps 1 and 2, as discussed in Sect. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#S6\">3</a>) to cluster-galaxy halos. The main contributions are listed in Table  <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#T1\">1</a> together with the basic scaling parameters used to model the contribution of 192 additional early-type cluster galaxies. All images detected in this small field are expected to be multiply imaged systems lensed by A1689. Our results below are fully consistent with this expectation, as discussed in Sect. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#S10\">4.3</a>. </p>\n<p>Table <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#T2\">2</a> presents the catalog of lensed images or sources identified in this field of view. Objects labeled LN in this table (Col. 1) correspond either to line emitters or multiple images lacking a counterpart in the reference catalog based on the <i>F775W </i>image. When the image or source was known before, its previous identification is given in Col. 2. Line fluxes were measured after subtracting the underlying continuum. Line profiles were fitted using MPDAF tools (Piqueras et al., in prep.). A double-Gaussian profile was adopted to fit Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> lines, combining two half Gaussian to better mimic the asymmetric profiles. For Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emitters, we adopted the maximum of the line as reference for redshift determinations. Figures <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F3\">3</a> and <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F4\">4</a> display the extracted spectra for all images after subtracting underlying continuum, grouped by lensing systems. Figure <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F5\">5</a> displays the distribution of emission-line fluxes versus redshift measured for the brightest emission lines (usually Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span>) versus redshift for the 21 galaxies found behind A1689. We note that multiply imaged sources are counted only once in this diagram, and only the brightest line is shown for a given source. The median lens-corrected flux is <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span><span class=\"simple-math\">1.4 &#215; 10<sup>-18</sup></span> erg/s/cm<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>. This illustrates the effective depth achieved in this survey based on a relatively modest amount of exposure time. </p>\n<p>\n        <a name=\"F3\"></a><div class=\"inset\"><table><tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F3.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15-fig3_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F3.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 3</span></a>\n            <p>Extracted spectra of all multiply imaged systems identified in the MUSE field of view at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8804; 3</span>, ordered according to increasing redshift, following the identifications in Table <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#T2\">2</a>. Continuum emission has been subtracted in all cases. The flux for counter-image LN20, extracted within a BCG, has been multiplied by a factor of 3 to improve readability. </p>\n          </td>\n</tr></table></div>\n      </p>\n<p>\n        <a name=\"F4\"></a><div class=\"inset\"><table><tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F4.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15-fig4_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F4.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 4</span></a>\n            <p>Same as in Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F3\">3</a> for multiply imaged systems at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8805; 3</span>. The gray area corresponds to a strong emission-line residual.</p>\n          </td>\n</tr></table></div>\n      </p>\n<p>\n        <a name=\"T2\"></a><div class=\"inset\"><div class=\"ligne\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/T2.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Table 2</span></a>\n            <p> Catalog of images identified behind the lensing cluster A1689 within the field of view of MUSE. </p>\n          </div></div>\n      </p>\n<h3 class=\"sec2\">\n<a name=\"S8\"></a>4.1. Results on previously known systems</h3>\n<p>Our MUSE survey has produced some interesting results on previously known systems in this field, in particular those exhibiting emission lines. We summarize these below. </p>\n<p>\n          <ul class=\"dash\">\n            <li>\n              \n              <p><i>System</i><i> 1 (619(1c) and L1f)</i>: one of the most\n                spectacular sources in this field is the Sextet Arc, corresponding to six separate\n                images of a strongly lensed LBGs at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 3.038</span>. <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2007ApJ...665..921F\" target=\"_blank\">(Frye et al.\n                  2007)</a>. Two images of the source are present in the MUSE field of view,\n                namely 1c and 1f. As shown by <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2007ApJ...665..921F\" target=\"_blank\">Frye et al.\n                  (2007)</a>, this galaxy exhibits a complex behavior that is highlighted by\n                magnification, providing an enhanced spatial resolution. The spectrum is dominated\n                by absorption in image 1a, displaying a complex Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> profile across the\n                galaxy, whereas a strong Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emission is found in image 1c. We here\n                confirm the redshift found for 1c and provide an additional proof of the reality of\n                this arc by confirming the Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emission of 1f. Before our survey, only a\n                photometric redshift was available for this image (see C10). In addition to this\n                result, an extended emission is also observed associated with 619(1c), with two main\n                  Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> extensions labeled LN23 and LN24 in Table\n                  <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#T2\">2</a>, as shown in Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F6\">6</a>. Given the location of 1f within the BCG region and its smaller\n                magnification, the counter images of LN23 and LN24 could not be detected. </p>\n            </li>\n            <li>\n              \n              <p><i>System</i><i> 4 (750(4a), 518(4b), and L4e)</i>: this\n                five-image system was described for the first time by L07, who provided a first\n                spectroscopic <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> =\n                  1.1</span>, in agreement with the photometric redshifts derived by C10.\n                A precise spectroscopic redshift was used by <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2010Sci...329..924J\" target=\"_blank\">Jullo et al.\n                  (2010)</a>, fully consistent with the present value. We here\n                spectroscopically confirm the system as being the multiple image of a source at\n                  <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> =\n                  1.164</span>, based on the detection of the same identical emission-line\n                doublet of [OII]3727 in the three images included in the MUSE field of view. </p>\n            </li>\n            <li>\n              <p><i>System</i><i> 7 (1379(7b), 1401, and LN16)</i>: the multiply\n                imaged system 7 was previously identified by <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2002ApJ...568..558F\" target=\"_blank\">Frye et al.\n                  (2002)</a> and later discussed by L07 and C10, who provided a photometric\n                and lensing-motivated identification for 7b. <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2002ApJ...568..558F\" target=\"_blank\">Frye et al.\n                  (2002)</a> and <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2011MNRAS.413..643R\" target=\"_blank\">Richard et al.\n                  (2011)</a> reported a redshift <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 4.860</span> for the 7a component, which is\n                located outside the MUSE field, based on the detection of Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emission for the\n                former and the [OII]3727 in the near-IR for the latter. Here we confirm the nature\n                of this system, with a spectroscopic redshift <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 4.874</span> for 7b,\n                based on a strong emission-line identified as Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span>. The emission\n                region seems to extend beyond the image seen on HST data, toward the neighboring\n                source 1401, as shown in Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F7\">7</a>. We note that\n                there is a difference in redshift of <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>0.011 (<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#948;v</i> ~ 560</span> km&#8201;s<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>-1</sup></span>) between the 7b\n                component reported here and the 7a component (using air wavelength reference for all\n                measurements to be consistent), which cannot be easily explained. The extended\n                  Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emission in this source might be sampled\n                differently in the two images. In addition, we confirm the spectroscopic redshift of\n                a counter-image located within the BCG area, labeled LN16 in Table <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#T2\">2</a>. Our results are fully consistent with a\n                three-image system, as suggested by previous authors. </p>\n              <p>\n                <a name=\"F5\"></a><div class=\"inset\"><table><tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F5.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15-fig5_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F5.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 5</span></a>\n                    <p>Distribution of emission-line fluxes measured for the brightest\n                      emission-lines versus redshift for the 21 sources found behind A1689, with and\n                      without correction for lensing magnification. The lines used are given in Col.\n                      3 of Table <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#T2\">2</a> (Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> at\n                        <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8805;\n                        3</span>). The horizontal dashed line indicates the median\n                      lens-corrected flux value. Multiply imaged sources are counted once in this\n                      diagram. </p>\n                  </td>\n</tr></table></div>\n              </p>\n              <p>\n                <a name=\"F6\"></a><div class=\"inset\"><table><tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F6.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15-fig6_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F6.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 6</span></a>\n                    <p>Color image of A1689 obtained by combining <i>F475W</i>,\n                        <i>F775W</i>, and <i>F850LP </i>HST/ACS images using a\n                      logarithmic scale, showing a 6.3<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span><span class=\"simple-math\">&#215;</span> 4.2<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span> region around 619(1c) and its extended\n                      emission. Circles have diameters of 0.60<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span>, close to the FWHM\n                      seeing measured in the MUSE data. Cyan isocontours display flux levels for\n                        Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emission, from 0.5 to <span class=\"simple-math\">2 &#215; 10<sup>-19</sup></span>\n                        erg/s/cm<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>/pix<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>, with bins of <span class=\"simple-math\">0.5 &#215; 10<sup>-19</sup></span>\n                        erg/s/cm<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>/pix<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>.</p>\n                  </td>\n</tr></table></div>\n              </p>\n              <p>\n                <a name=\"F7\"></a><div class=\"inset\"><table><tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F7.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15-fig7_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F7.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 7</span></a>\n                    <p>Color image of A1689 obtained by combining <i>F475W</i>,\n                        <i>F775W</i>, and <i>F850LP </i>HST/ACS images using a\n                      logarithmic scale, showing a 6.3<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span><span class=\"simple-math\">&#215;</span> 4.2<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span> region around 1379 and 1401. Circles have\n                      diameters of 0.60<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span>, which is close to the FWHM seeing measured\n                      in the MUSE data. Cyan isocontours display flux levels for\n                        Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emission from 0.5 to <span class=\"simple-math\">18 &#215; 10<sup>-19</sup></span>\n                        erg/s/cm<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>/pix<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>, with bins of <span class=\"simple-math\">1 &#215; 10<sup>-19</sup></span>\n                        erg/s/cm<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>/pix<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>. </p>\n                  </td>\n</tr></table></div>\n              </p>\n            </li>\n            <li>\n              \n              <p><i>System</i><i> 17 (L17a)</i>: we spectroscopically confirm\n                the redshift of the three-image system 17 in C10 as <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 2.661</span>, based on\n                identifying the emission-line doublet of CIII]1909. This value agrees well with the\n                photometric and lensing redshifts around <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 2.7 &#177; 0.5</span> estimated by L07 and C10. </p>\n            </li>\n            <li>\n              \n              <p><i>System</i><i> 26 (L26b)</i>: we spectroscopically confirm\n                the redshift of the three-image system 26 in C10 as <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> =</span> 0.959, based on\n                identifying the emission-line doublet of [OII]3727. This value agrees excellently\n                well with the photometric and lensing redshifts <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 0.9 &#177; 0.2</span>\n                estimated by C10. In addition, the counter-image 26c in C10, which has a smaller\n                magnification factor of <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>3.2, is also detected as a faint emission seen in the 3D MUSE\n                cube, but it is too faint to be successfully extracted. These results fully confirm\n                the lensing system. </p>\n            </li>\n            <li>\n              <p><i>System</i><i> 46 (944(46a) and LN22)</i>: this highly\n                magnified double-image system was reported in C10 with uncertain photometric\n                redshifts for the two images. Here we measure a redshift <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 3.483</span> based on an\n                emission line identified as Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span>. The two objects showing this emission on\n                the 1.5<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span>\n                diameter aperture are located side by side, but the emission line is clearly\n                centered on LN22, lacking a clear counterpart in the HST/ACS images, as shown in\n                Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F8\">8</a>. Based on these measurements, it is more\n                likely a three-image system, with two images located within the MUSE field. The\n                fainter counter-images are expected to be located within the central (noisy) region,\n                with fluxes (<span class=\"simple-math\">~</span><span class=\"simple-math\">1 &#215;\n                  10<sup>-18</sup></span> erg/s/cm<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>) that are too faint to be\n                detected with a significant S/N in this area. </p>\n              <p>\n                <a name=\"F8\"></a><div class=\"inset\"><table><tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F8.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15-fig8_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F8.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 8</span></a>\n                    <p>Color image of A1689 obtained by combining <i>F475W</i>,\n                        <i>F775W</i>, and <i>F850LP </i>HST/ACS images using a\n                      logarithmic scale, showing a 3.7<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span><span class=\"simple-math\">&#215;</span> 2.45<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span> region around 944 and LN22. Circles have\n                      diameters of 0.60<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span>, which is close to the FWHM seeing measured\n                      in the MUSE data. Cyan isocontours display flux levels for\n                        Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emission from 0.3 to <span class=\"simple-math\">8 &#215; 10<sup>-19</sup></span>\n                        erg/s/cm<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>/pix<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>, with bins of <span class=\"simple-math\">1.25 &#215; 10<sup>-20</sup></span>\n                        erg/s/cm<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>/pix<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>. The brightest source seen in the HST image\n                      is likely to be a cluster galaxy, but no spectroscopic redshift could be\n                      determined for it.</p>\n                  </td>\n</tr></table></div>\n              </p>\n            </li>\n            <li>\n              \n              <p><i>System</i><i> 50 (L50a, 588(50b) and L50c)</i>: MUSE\n                spectroscopy has allowed us to confirm this spectacular three-image system based on\n                the detection of a strong emission-line identified as Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> for a source at\n                  <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> =\n                  4.274</span>, and seen in the three images available in this field.\n                Previous photometric redshifts reported by C10 were highly inaccurate (between\n                  <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> =\n                  2.2</span> and 3.2). Therefore, these observations allow us to confirm\n                the redshift and nature of this system. </p>\n            </li>\n          </ul>Unfortunately, only a tentative spectroscopic redshift could be obtained for the long arcs located southeast in Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F1\">1</a>, namely 8a and 8b in C10, despite a strong magnification. These arcs were identified by C10 as two images of the same source, with photometric and lensing redshifts of <span class=\"simple-math\">1.8 &#177; 0.5</span> and 2.22, respectively. Extracted spectra are very noisy, and strong spectral features such as [OII]3727 and Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> are not expected within the MUSE wavelength domain. Here we propose a tentative redshift of <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 2.661</span>, mainly based on several consistent absorption features, such as CII 1334, SiIV 1393 <span class=\"simple-math\">+</span> OIV 1402, FeII 1608, and AlII 1670. A faint emission-line is also detected in one of the portions of 8a, consistent with CIII]1909, but the S/N ratio is very low compared to the other line emitters discussed here. A longer exposure time and further investigation are needed to fully confirm this redshift. </p>\n<h3 class=\"sec2\">\n<a name=\"S9\"></a>4.2. New multiply imaged sources behind A1689</h3>\n<p>As a result of this survey, 14 new background sources were identified behind A1689, as reported in Table <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#T2\">2</a>. All of them generate multiply imaged systems, identified from <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>N</i> = 51</span> to 64 (in continuity with respect to C10). In two cases, we were able to spectroscopically confirm the identification of (at least) two such images: </p>\n<p>\n          <ul class=\"dash\">\n            <li>\n              <p><i>System</i><i> 51 (1339 and LN20)</i>: 1339 is a highly\n                magnified image of a source at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> =</span> 0.775, based on the identification of\n                several emission-lines, mainly [OIII]5007, 4959, H<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#946;</i></span>, H<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#947;</i></span>, NeIII, the\n                [OII]3727 doublet, and MgII. LN20 is an image extracted within the BCG area and\n                displays the same (main) emission lines. These two images are consistent with a new\n                three-image system, with two images located within the MUSE field of view. In this\n                case, magnifications affecting 1339 and LN20 are <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>13 and <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>2, respectively, which agrees well\n                with the relative line fluxes. The third image is found as expected in the field\n                that is covered by HST images, with <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>m</i></span>(775W) = 25.1 and magnification\n                  <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>5. </p>\n            </li>\n            <li>\n              <p><i>System</i><i> 52 (1028, 1045 and LN12)</i>: 1028 is a highly\n                magnified image of a source at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 3.112</span>, based on the identification of\n                  Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> and CIV seen in emission.\n                  Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> in emission is also seen at the same redshift\n                in a region associated with 1045 (in the close neighborhood of 1028), as shown in\n                Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F9\">9</a>. The system is consistent with a new\n                three-image source, with two images located within the MUSE field of view, namely\n                1028 (and its Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> extension 1045), and LN12, which were\n                extracted within the BCG area. The third image is identified in the field covered by\n                HST images, with <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>m</i></span>(775W) = 26.9 and magnification\n                  <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>4. </p>\n            </li>\n          </ul>Some newly discovered sources in this field deserve a special mention. </p>\n<p>\n          \n          <a name=\"F9\"></a><div class=\"inset\"><table><tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F9.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15-fig9_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F9.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 9</span></a>\n              <p>Color image of A1689 obtained by combining <i>F475W</i>, <i>F775W</i>, and <i>F850LP </i>HST/ACS images using a logarithmic scale, showing a 6.3<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span><span class=\"simple-math\">&#215;</span> 4.2<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span> region around 1028 and 1045. Circles have diameters of 0.60<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8242;&#8242;</span>, which is close to the FWHM seeing measured in the MUSE data. Cyan isocontours display flux levels for Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emission from 0.5 to <span class=\"simple-math\">35 &#215; 10<sup>-19</sup></span> erg/s/cm<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>/pix<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>, with bins of <span class=\"simple-math\">2 &#215; 10<sup>-20</sup></span> erg/s/cm<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>/pix<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>.</p>\n            </td>\n</tr></table></div>\n        </p>\n<p>\n          <ul class=\"dash\">\n            <li>\n              <p><i>Systems</i><i> 53, 54, and 55 (LN9, 1404, and 835)</i>:\n                these three images display a similar redshift <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> ~ 3.18</span>. However,\n                based on the lensing model, they cannot be reconciled with a multiple-image system.\n                LN9 and 1404 are two independent systems with three multiple images each, two of\n                them within the MUSE field, namely the image detected and another counter-image\n                within the BCG region <span class=\"simple-math\">thatisaboutfive</span> times fainter for LN9 and de-magnified\n                  (<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#956;</i> ~\n                  0.03</span>) for 1404. A candidate third image could be extracted for\n                system 54 at the expected position in the field covered by HST images, close to a\n                bright cluster galaxy, with <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>m</i></span>(775W) = 27.4. In contrast, there is no\n                obvious counterpart for the faint continuum emission associated with LN9 despite a\n                1.2 times larger magnification, but the image is expected in the close neighborhood\n                of a particularly crowded region. 835 is more likely a double-image system, with a\n                de-magnified counter-image located within the BCG region. </p>\n            </li>\n            <li>\n              <p><i>System</i><i> 56 (LN10)</i>: this image displays the largest\n                magnification of the sample (<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#956;</i> ~ 75</span>). It is most likely a new three-image\n                source at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> ~\n                  3.419</span>, with two images located within the MUSE field of view. The\n                magnification of the counter-image expected within the BCG area is <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#956;</i> ~ 9</span>, yielding a\n                flux below <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span><span class=\"simple-math\">2 &#215;\n                  10<sup>-18</sup></span> erg/s/cm<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>, which is too faint to be\n                detected in this area. There is an extremely faint object in the field covered by\n                HST images, with <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>m</i></span>(775W) <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span> 28 and magnification <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>8, which is a good candidate to the\n                third image. </p>\n            </li>\n          </ul>For all newly discovered galaxies, in addition to those discussed above, we checked the consistency of the lensing configuration by identifying possible counter-image candidates predicted in the field covered by HST data. For images lacking a detection in the continuum (systems 57, 58, 61, 63, and 64), there is no obvious counter-image in HST data. The only exception is system 62, for which a faint arclet is detected at the predicted position, with <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>m</i></span>(775W) = 27.6 and magnification <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>15.5, that is, a larger magnification than in the image seen in the MUSE field. There is no obvious counter-part for the faint systems 59 and 60. In the first case, the magnification is expected to be 1.2 times larger, but the image is predicted in the close neighborhood of a bright cluster galaxy. In the second case, the counter-image is expected to be <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>0.4 mag fainter. </p>\n<h3 class=\"sec2\">\n<a name=\"S10\"></a>4.3. Discussion</h3>\n<p>All background sources detected within the MUSE field of view correspond to multiply imaged systems. The spectroscopic images described above are consistent with this fact. In most cases, they correspond to three- or five-image systems with at least two images located within the MUSE field. The detection of counterparts within the BCG area, with observed line fluxes expected to be around or below <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span><span class=\"simple-math\">2 &#215; 10<sup>-18</sup></span> erg/s/cm<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span>, is simply unfeasible. Therefore, in the majority of cases presented above, there is no spectroscopic confirmation of the multiple system, and this is a very common situation in the literature (i.e., the spectroscopic redshift being available for only one of the images in a multiple system). However, for sources exhibiting a continuum (i.e., detected in HST images), we have identified possible counterparts outside the field of MUSE. The mass-model used in this analysis is accurate enough to permit a good determination of magnification factors and related quantities and to identify multiple systems. A new revised mass-model, including all the new multiple images discussed above, will be presented in a coming paper (Richard et al., in preparation). </p>\n<p>Compared to the sample of 26 bright well-behaved Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emitters observed by MUSE in the HDFS at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8805; 2.9</span> and displaying extended Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emission <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2015A&amp;A...575A..75B,%202015arXiv150905143W\" target=\"_blank\">(i.e., isolated, non-AGN galaxies Bacon et al. 2015; Wisotzki et al. 2016)</a>, our sample is intrinsically fainter, with Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> luminosities ranging between 40.5 <span class=\"simple-math\">&#8818;</span> log(<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>L</i></span>)[erg&#8201;s<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>-1</sup></span>] <span class=\"simple-math\">&#8818;</span> 42.5 after correction for magnification. As a result of the relatively short exposure time and because these observations were performed close to the extended halo of BCG in the cluster core, we do not discuss the extended Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emission around individual sources here. However, such an emission is clearly observed in at least four cases as described above (systems 1c, 7b, 46a, and 52; see Figs. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F6\">6</a> to <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F9\">9</a>). </p>\n<p>When we compare the distribution of lens-corrected Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> luminosities for the 17 galaxies found behind A1689 at <span class=\"simple-math\">3 &#8818; <i>z</i> &#8818; 7</span> to a compilation of representative spectroscopic samples from the literature (see Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F10\">10</a>), the complementarity between classical blank-field and lensing studies is obvious. Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emitters observed by MUSE in lensing clusters nicely extend the accessible domain in luminosity between one and two orders of magnitude beyond classical LAE surveys. The luminosities reached here are comparable with those attained by <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2008ApJ...681..856R\" target=\"_blank\">Rauch et al. (2008)</a> in their <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>90h exposure with VLT/FORS2 (gray triangles in Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F10\">10</a>). The present sample also reaches fainter limits than the survey conducted on the HDFS by <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2015A&amp;A...575A..75B\" target=\"_blank\">Bacon et al. (2015)</a>, in particular at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8819; 4</span>, which is due to the specific pointing covering the highest magnification regime in this particularly efficient cluster. </p>\n<p>\n          \n          <a name=\"F10\"></a><div class=\"inset\"><table><tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F10.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15-fig10_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F10.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 10</span></a>\n              <p>Distribution of lens-corrected Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> luminosities for the 17 galaxies found behind A1689 at <span class=\"simple-math\">3 &#8804; <i>z</i> &#8804; 7</span> (red squares), as compared to <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2015A&amp;A...575A..75B\" target=\"_blank\">Bacon et al. (2015)</a> (blue diamonds), and to a compilation of representative samples of LAE from the literature (gray symbols): <span class=\"simple-math\">2 &#8818; <i>z</i> &#8818; 3.8</span><a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2011ApJ...736...31B\" target=\"_blank\">(Blanc et al. 2011)</a> (HETDEX Pilot Survey), <span class=\"simple-math\">2.7 &#8818; <i>z</i> &#8818; 3.8</span> (gray triangles) <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2008ApJ...681..856R\" target=\"_blank\">(Rauch et al. 2008)</a>, <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> ~ 4.9</span><a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2009ApJ...696..546S\" target=\"_blank\">(Shioya et al. 2009)</a>, <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> ~ 5.7</span><a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2006PASJ...58..313S,2008ApJS..176..301O,2012ApJ...744..149H,2010ApJ...725..394H\" target=\"_blank\">(Shimasaku et al. 2006; Ouchi et al. 2008; Henry et al. 2012; Hu et al. 2010)</a>, and <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> ~ 6.5</span><a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2010ApJ...723..869O,2010ApJ...725..394H,2011ApJ...734..119K\" target=\"_blank\">(Ouchi et al. 2010; Hu et al. 2010; Kashikawa et al. 2011)</a>. </p>\n            </td>\n</tr></table></div>\n        </p>\n<p>A high magnification value also translates into a small effective surface or volume covered by the survey on the corresponding source planes. To evaluate this effect, we computed the effective volume covered by the survey in the different redshift bins from <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> ~ 3.5</span> to <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> ~ 6.5</span>, with redshift slices of <span class=\"simple-math\">&#916;<i>z</i> = 0.5</span>. A mask was used to remove the areas contaminated by the central BCGs, where faint sources typically below a few <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span><span class=\"simple-math\">&#215;</span>10<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>-18</sup></span> erg/s/cm<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>2</sup></span> could not be detected. This mask accounts for <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>11% of the total surface. We integrated the effective volume outside the mask using the same approach as in <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2006A&amp;A...456..861R\" target=\"_blank\">Richard et al. (2006)</a>, that is, the surface of each pixel was reduced by the corresponding magnification (depending on position and redshift). We used Lenstool and the same lensing model as in Sect. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#S6\">3</a> to derive the magnification maps for each redshift slice.
