The total effective covolume obtained in this way in the field of view of MUSE is <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>145 Mpc<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>3</sup></span> at <span class=\"simple-math\">3 &#8818; <i>z</i> &#8818; 7</span>, whereas it is <span class=\"simple-math\">~</span>2300 Mpc<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>3</sup></span> in a blank field. </p>\n<p>Figure <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F11\">11</a> displays the comparison between the density of sources obtained in this way within the whole <span class=\"simple-math\">3 &#8818; <i>z</i> &#8818; 7</span> interval, and expectations based on the extrapolation of the luminosity function (LF) toward the low-luminosity regime covered by the present survey. Luminosity bins were defined to keep at least three sources per bin, and they are independent. Given the small number of sources, we did not introduce any correction for incompleteness at this stage, knowing that incompleteness is expected to affect in particular the faintest bins in Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F11\">11</a>. Error bars in this figure include Poisson noise statistics that affect the number of galaxies found in a given luminosity bin, as well as an estimate of the field-to-field variance, added in quadrature. Field-to-field variance was estimated using the public cosmic variance calculator by <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2008ApJ...676..767T\" target=\"_blank\">Trenti &amp; Stiavelli (2008)</a>. The error budget is clearly dominated by Poisson noise in this case. </p>\n<p>Given the intrinsic low luminosities in our sample, we are particularly sensitive to the value of the slope parameter <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span>, for which a constant value is assumed in other surveys presented in Figs. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F10\">10</a> and <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#F11\">11</a>, where the fit is only sensitive to <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>L</i><sup>&#8727;</sup></span> and the normalization. Despite these caveats discussed above regarding the small size of this sample, the density of intrinsically faint sources observed in this field is roughly consistent with the steepest values used by the different authors to fit their data, namely <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i> &#8804; &#8722;1.5</span>, and inconsistent with flatter values of <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span>. Any correction for completeness in the faintest bins will exacerbate this trend. This result still needs further investigation to be confirmed, using larger samples of LAE in this low-luminosity domain. A full analysis of the LF for the faint Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emitters behind lensing clusters will be presented elsewhere in a forthcoming paper. </p>\n<p>\n          \n          <a name=\"F11\"></a><div class=\"inset\"><table><tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F11.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15-fig11_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/F11.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 11</span></a>\n              <p>Comparison between the density of sources observed at <span class=\"simple-math\">3 &#8804; <i>z</i> &#8804; 7</span> behind A1689 and expectations based on the extrapolation of the LF toward the low-luminosity regime covered by the present survey. References are given in the figure for different redshifts. Solid lines display the steepest slopes adopted for the LF fit: <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i> = &#8722;1.7</span> for <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2011ApJ...734..119K\" target=\"_blank\">Kashikawa et al. (2011)</a> and <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2011ApJ...736...31B\" target=\"_blank\">Blanc et al. (2011)</a>, <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i> = &#8722;2.0</span> for <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2009ApJ...696..546S\" target=\"_blank\">Shioya et al. (2009)</a>, and <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i> = &#8722;1.6</span> for <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2007ApJ...671.1227D\" target=\"_blank\">Dawson et al. (2007)</a>. Dashed and dotted lines correspond to <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i> = &#8722;1.5</span> and <span class=\"simple-math\">&#8722;</span>1.3 for <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2011ApJ...734..119K\" target=\"_blank\">Kashikawa et al. (2011)</a> and <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i> = &#8722;1.5</span> and <span class=\"simple-math\">&#8722;</span>1.0 for <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2009ApJ...696..546S\" target=\"_blank\">Shioya et al. (2009)</a>. Error bars include Poisson noise statistics and field-to-field variance (see text). </p>\n            </td>\n</tr></table></div>\n        </p>\n<h2 class=\"sec\">\n<a name=\"S11\"></a>5. Conclusions</h2>\n<p>To summarize, these are the main results we obtained: </p>\n<p>\n        <ul class=\"dash\">\n          <li>\n            \n            <p>Based on guided-and-manual and automated (blind) approaches, a census of sources was obtained in the field of MUSE, most of which are cluster galaxies. The spectroscopic census is complete out to <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>m</i></span>(775W) <span class=\"simple-math\">&lt;</span> 21.5. The spectroscopic sample includes 63 cluster galaxies with secure redshifts (49 of them with <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>m</i></span>(775W) <span class=\"simple-math\">&lt;</span> 21.5). The velocity distribution of cluster galaxies is more complex than the smooth Gaussian distribution found for this cluster on larger scales, with a main cluster component with <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#963;</i> = 1200</span> km&#8201;s<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>-1</sup></span>, and the signature of the NE group component, with <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#963;</i> = 600</span> km&#8201;s<span class=\"simple-math\"><sup>-1</sup></span>. This demonstrates that MUSE data are able to catch the small-scale substructure in particularly dense environments, a difficult exercise for usual multi-slit spectrographs. This result supports the mass-model method adopted by L07 and used throughout the paper to retrieve lens-corrected quantities. </p>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n            \n            <p>We are able to confirm 12 images for background sources that correspond to 7 different lensed galaxies between <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> = 0.95</span> and 5.0 of the 28 different lensed galaxies known or suspected within the MUSE field of view. In addition, 14 new galaxies were spectroscopically identified in this area thanks to MUSE data, with redshifts ranging between 0.8 and 6.2, the majority of them identified based on their Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emission. All background sources detected within the MUSE field of view correspond to multiply imaged systems, in most cases three- or five-image systems with at least two images located within the MUSE field. </p>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n            \n            <p>In total, 17 sources are found at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8805; 3</span> based on their Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emission, with Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> luminosities ranging between 40.5<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8818;</span>log(Ly<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span>)<span class=\"simple-math\">&#8818;</span>42.5 after correction for magnification. Four of these systems display extended Lyman-<span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i></span> emission. Our sample is intrinsically fainter than the usual samples available in the literature, in particular at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8805; 4</span>, and comparable to the faintest samples currently available at lower redshifts <a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2015A&amp;A...575A..75B,%202015arXiv150905143W\" target=\"_blank\">(e.g., the sample Lyman-&#945; emitters observed by MUSE in the HDFS at z&#8805;2.9  Bacon et al. 2015; Wisotzki et al. 2016)</a>. Given the intrinsically low luminosities, this sample is particularly sensitive to the slope of the LF toward the faintest-end. The density of sources obtained in this survey is roughly consistent with a steep value of <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i> &#8804; &#8722;1.5</span>, although this result still needs further investigation. </p>\n          </li>\n        </ul>\n      </p>\n<p>These results illustrate the efficiency of MUSE in characterizing lensing clusters on one hand, and studying faint and distant populations of galaxies on the other hand. In particular, our current survey of lensing clusters is expected to provide a unique census of sources responsible for the reionization in a limited representative volume at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> ~ 4&#8722;7</span>. </p>\n    <h2 class=\"sec\">\n<a name=\"ack\"></a>Acknowledgments</h2>\n<p>We thank O. Czoske for providing unpublished spectroscopic data on A1689. Part of this work was supported by the French CNRS. This work has been carried out thanks to the support of the OCEVU Labex (ANR-11-LABX-0060) and the A*MIDEX project (ANR-11-IDEX-0001-02) funded by the &#8220;Investissements d&#8217;Avenir&#8221; French government program managed by the ANR. Partially funded by the ERC starting grant CALENDS (J.R., V.P., B.C.), and the Agence Nationale de la recherche bearing the references ANR-09-BLAN-0234 and ANR-13-BS05-0010-02 (FOGHAR). Based on observations made with ESO Telescopes at the La Silla Paranal Observatory under programme ID 60.A-9100(B). We thank all the staff at Paranal Observatory for their valuable support during the commissioning of MUSE. Also based on observations made with the NASA/ESA <i>Hubble </i>Space Telescope (PID 9289). </p>\n    <h2 class=\"sec\">\n<a name=\"ref\"></a>References</h2>\n    <div id=\"content\">\n        <ol target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 1</span></a>\n              <p>Color image of A1689 obtained by combining <i>F475W</i>, <i>F775W</i>, and <i>F850LP </i>HST/ACS images using a logarithmic scale. The footprint of the MUSE field is displayed together with the sources spectroscopically identified in this field: cluster galaxies (red), stars (magenta), background galaxies at <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8804; 3</span> (cyan), and <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>z</i> &#8805; 3</span> (yellow). Cluster galaxies that were manually extracted are labeled CG. Objects labeled LN correspond to either line emitters or multiple images lacking a counterpart in the reference catalog based on the <i>F775W </i>image (see text for details). North is up, east is left. A tentative spectroscopic redshift was also obtained for the long southeast arcs in this field, namely 8a and 8b in C10 (see discussion in Sect. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/06/aa27913-15/aa27913-15.html#S8\">4.1</a>). name=\"citation_online_date\" content=\"2016/04/28\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_publication_date\" content=\"2016/06/01\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_volume\" content=\"590\">\n  <meta content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/pdf/2016/06/aa27913-15.pdf\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_issn\" content=\"0004-6361\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_issn\" content=\"1432-0746\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_language\" content=\"en\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"gravitational lensing: strong\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"galaxies: high-redshift\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"galaxies: clusters: individual: Abell 1689\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_article_type\" content=\"Research Article\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_abstract\" lang=\"en\" content=\"&lt;i&gt;Context. &lt;i/&gt;This paper presents the results obtained with the Multi Unit Spectroscopic Explorer (MUSE) for the core of the lensing cluster Abell 1689, as part of MUSE\u2019s commissioning at the ESO Very Large Telescope.&lt;i&gt;Aims. &lt;i/&gt;Integral-field observations with MUSE provide a unique view of the central 1 \u00d7 1 arcmin&lt;sup&gt;2&lt;sup/&gt; region at intermediate spectral resolution in the visible domain, allowing us to conduct a complete census of both cluster galaxies and lensed background sources.&lt;i&gt;Methods. &lt;i/&gt;We performed a spectroscopic analysis of all sources found in the MUSE data cube. Two hundred and eighty-two objects were systematically extracted from the cube based on a guided-and-manual approach. We also tested three different tools for the automated detection and extraction of line emitters. Cluster galaxies and lensed sources were identified based on their spectral features. We investigated the multiple-image configuration for all known sources in the field. &lt;i&gt;Results. &lt;i/&gt;Previous to our survey, 28 different lensed galaxies displaying 46 multiple images were known in the MUSE field of view, most of them were detected through photometric redshifts and lensing considerations. Of these, we spectroscopically confirm 12 images based on their emission lines, corresponding to 7 different lensed galaxies between &lt;i&gt;z&lt;i/&gt; = 0.95 and 5.0. In addition, 14 new galaxies have been spectroscopically identified in this area thanks to MUSE data, with redshifts ranging between 0.8 and 6.2. All background sources detected within the MUSE field of view correspond to multiple-imaged systems lensed by A1689. Seventeen sources in total are found at &lt;i&gt;z&lt;i/&gt; \u2265 3 based on their Lyman-&lt;i&gt;\u03b1&lt;i/&gt; emission, with Lyman-&lt;i&gt;\u03b1&lt;i/&gt; luminosities ranging between 40.5 \u2272 log\u2009(Ly&lt;i&gt;\u03b1&lt;i/&gt;) \u2272 42.5 after correction for magnification. This sample is particularly sensitive to the slope of the luminosity function toward the faintest end. The density of sources obtained in this survey is consistent with a steep value of &lt;i&gt;\u03b1&lt;i/&gt; \u2264 \u22121.5, although this result still needs further investigation. &lt;i&gt;Conclusions. &lt;i/&gt;These results illustrate the efficiency of MUSE in characterizing lensing clusters on one hand and in studying faint and distant populations of galaxies on the other hand. In particular, our current survey of lensing clusters is expected to provide a unique census of sources responsible for the reionization in a representative volume at &lt;i&gt;z&lt;i/&gt; ~ 4\u22127.\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_reference\" content=\"citation_author=A. Alavi;citation_author=B. Siana;citation_author=J. Richard;citation_publication_date=2014;citation_journal_title=ApJ;citation_volume=780;citation_firstpage=143;\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_reference\" content=\"citation_author=H. Atek;citation_author=J. Richard;citation_author=J.-P. <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"galaxies: clusters: individual: Abell 1689\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_article_type\" content=\"Research Article\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_abstract\" lang=\"en\" content=\"&lt;i&gt;Context. &lt;i/&gt;This paper presents the results obtained with the Multi Unit Spectroscopic Explorer (MUSE) for the core of the lensing cluster Abell 1689, as part of MUSE\u2019s commissioning at the ESO Very Large Telescope.&lt;i&gt;Aims. &lt;i/&gt;Integral-field observations with MUSE provide a unique view of the central 1 \u00d7 1 arcmin&lt;sup&gt;2&lt;sup/&gt; region at intermediate spectral resolution in the visible domain, allowing us to conduct a complete census of both cluster galaxies and lensed background sources.&lt;i&gt;Methods. &lt;i/&gt;We performed a spectroscopic analysis of all sources found in the MUSE data cube. Two hundred and eighty-two objects were systematically extracted from the cube based on a guided-and-manual approach. We also tested three different tools for the automated detection and extraction of line emitters. Cluster galaxies and lensed sources were identified based on their spectral features. We investigated the multiple-image configuration for all known sources in the field. &lt;i&gt;Results. &lt;i/&gt;Previous to our survey, 28 different lensed galaxies displaying 46 multiple images were known in the MUSE field of view, most of them were detected through photometric redshifts and lensing considerations. Of these, we spectroscopically confirm 12 images based on their emission lines, corresponding to 7 different lensed galaxies between &lt;i&gt;z&lt;i/&gt; = 0.95 and 5.0. In addition, 14 new galaxies have been spectroscopically identified in this area thanks to MUSE data, with redshifts ranging between 0.8 and 6.2. All background sources detected within the MUSE field of view correspond to multiple-imaged systems lensed by A1689. Seventeen sources in total are found at &lt;i&gt;z&lt;i/&gt; \u2265 3 based on their Lyman-&lt;i&gt;\u03b1&lt;i/&gt; emission, with Lyman-&lt;i&gt;\u03b1&lt;i/&gt; luminosities ranging between 40.5 \u2272 log\u2009(Ly&lt;i&gt;\u03b1&lt;i/&gt;) \u2272 42.5 after correction for magnification. This sample is particularly sensitive to the slope of the luminosity function toward the faintest end. The density of sources obtained in this survey is consistent with a steep value of &lt;i&gt;\u03b1&lt;i/&gt; \u2264 \u22121.5, although this result still needs further investigation. &lt;i&gt;Conclusions. &lt;i/&gt;These results illustrate the efficiency of MUSE in characterizing lensing clusters on one hand and in studying faint and distant populations of galaxies on the other hand. In particular, our current survey of lensing clusters is expected to provide a unique census of sources responsible for the reionization in a representative volume at &lt;i&gt;z&lt;i/&gt; ~ 4\u22127.\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_reference\" content=\"citation_author=A. Alavi;citation_author=B. Siana;citation_author=J.
